\c BL-00   
\t Target audience and redemptive themes
\stg Bkgrnd (Bulgarian)
\bt Target audience: Pomak (the older generation)
\co The Pomatzi (plural of Pomak), or Bulgarian Muslims, are a Muslim minority people group in Bulgaria,
which is a mainly Bulgarian Orthodox Christian nation. The Pomatzi are ethnically Bulgarian, but their
ancestors were converted to Islam during the rule by the Ottoman Empire, which lasted from the
fifteenth till nineteenth century. Though in name they hold on to their Muslim identity, in practice they
have been largely influenced by Communism and tend to know very little about Islam. They also hold
animistic and folk-Islamic beliefs, especially the older generation. The Pomatzi live largely in the
southern part of Bulgaria and also in parts of Greece, Macedonia and Turkey.

\bt Redemptive theme: Relationship
\co Across the board, relationships appear to be very important to Bulgarians. People are very aware of
family ties, "everybody knows everybody", and interpersonal relations are prioritized. However, for
the older generation loneliness appears to be an issue as many have lost their spouses and their children
are often far away for work or study. With (the end of) Communism, materialism and individualism also
seem to have set in, resulting in more of an 'every man for himself' attitude. As for their image of God,
Communism has taught them there is no God and what they have learned about the religious God of their
(grand)parents, He is rather distant and more about rituals than personal relationship. In this story set,
we want to show God interacting with and relating to  people on a very personal and understandable
way. We also want to emphasize that God is with us.

\bt Redemptive theme: Trust
\co After Communism fell, Democracy did not bring what people might have hoped for. People are
thoroughly and explicitly disappointed in politics and have no faith in the government, which used to
take care of almost every aspect of their lives (work, education, faith, etc.). People feel that there is no
one looking after them any more, and they have to take care of themselves. This includes feeling
forgotten by God. There is a saying that goes something like "God helps, but He doesn't put food on the
table." In this story set, we want to show God's provision, faithfulness, and concern for people.

\co Crafter: GM - Orthodox/Atheist/Communist from a nearby Christian Village. Around 50 years old. Has
never read the Bible before, but has attended the Orth. church.
\co Backtranslator: IK - Not sure, maybe Atheist/Communist. Around 50 years old. From a nearby village.
Has read and heard a little about the Bible but not much. 30Jan09
\co Resources: Bulgarian bibles (Bulgarian Bible Association, Living Word, Orthodox), first crafted story
(by GM), slide show pictures (Sarah, is that correct?)
\co Test 1: ZK - early fifties, our people group, from M village, identifies herself as M but doesn't
practice, only knows about her religion from what her grandmother told her, semi-atheist
\co Test 2: RC - early thirties, our people group, from M parents who didn't practice, doesn't practice
herself, presumably atheist. 13Jul08
\co Test 3: ER - early twenties, our people group, from M village, M parents who didn't practice, materialist
but aware that something like God might exist, student. Retelling: Fairly accurate retelling. Got the
action and names in but left out almost everything God said, except the command to go. Left out the
promises, except that Abram would have posterity. Added details here and there ("Avram went out on a
walk and heard a voice", "Avram thought about it and decided to obey"). 26May09
\co Test 4: FH - mid twenties, our people group, from more concervative M village, M parents practice and
take their faith seriously, husband Turkish and very religious.

\dt 28/Sep/2009

\c BL-79
\t RICH YOUNG MAN
\stg S-by-S (Bulgarian) SH
\co Language: Bulgarian
\co Reason for having this story in the set: For the relationship theme, in this story we see Jesus
prioritizing relationship (with the children), and it says how Jesus liked the young ruler. Also, people
are very aware of "being a good person". In this story, Jesus says only God is good.
\co Crafter: GM
\co Backtranslator: IK
\co Resources used in crafting this story: Bulgarian Bible Living Word '06
\co Test 1: RC 21Aug09 
\co Test 2: ER and NR (NR only the last few) 22Sep09
\ln 79.01
\bt Children come to Isus and his students to touch Him. But Isus students take them away.
\anc mrk.10:13
\rtl1 The children come to Jesus and his students who want to touch Him. And Jesusí students become to chase
them away. 
\rtl2 A lot of children have come to Jesus to talk with him. Then his students have tried to chase them away, 
\ln 79.02
\bt And Isus says to leave them with Him because the Gods kingdom is for such.
\anc mrk.10:14
\rtl1 But He says them to leave them and He has blessed them, 
\rtl2 but Jesus has said to them to stop 
\ln 79.03
\bt Who doesnt accept the Gods kingdom as a child, he will never go into it. 
\co NP: "As a child" interpreted by backtranslator and testers as "while you are a litle child (age)".
\anc mrk.10:15
\rtl1 and said that from the childrenís age have to accept the Godís kingdom, because who hasnít accepted
from the young age, it become difficult later. 
\rtl2 because the children have to learn from their young age for some things and in that way to come in and
to learn about the Godís kingdom. And also He has said to the students that the Godís kingdom is
represented from children. 
\tst How does a child accept things, like presents, candy etc?
\tsta RC: Maybe Jesus is saying that a person has to be taught when he is young to be good, to not steal or lie,
to believe in God, to receive this faith and everything he teaches. Because if you teach them from the
beginning then when the children grow up they will be good people. When people are older and they
havent been taught as children, its a little harder maybe. Thats maybe what hes trying to say, they need
to be taught when theyre children to receive these things.
\tsta ER: With pleasure and joy.
\ln 79.04
\bt After that He blesses them.
\anc mrk.10:16
\rtl2 Then the children have become to speak with Jesus and He has blessed them. 
\tst What do you think he did or said to "bless them"
\tsta RC: Maybe he told them something good. (SH: Do you understand this word Blagoslavi (bless them) or is
it a little religious?) Its religious but Blago (means generous, good) it means he told something good.
\tsta ER: Like people normally bless a person. With blessings: he declares words over them and blesses. And
he 'crosses' them. (SH: What kind of words?) May God bless you.
\ln 79.05 
\bt A man meets Isus on the street and says to Him: Generous teacher, how can I inherit the life
forever?
\anc mrk.10:17
\co NP: Generous - The word for "blag" used here was intended to mean "very good" (better than just good,
or dober), but was mistaken first for "mlad" (young) and translated differently. Should be changed to
"dober". RECRAFT??
\cn Bulgarian-English Dictionary (Blag - gentle, kind, sweet character, good.)
\rtl1 After that Jesus meets a man who also says to Jesus that he wants to be (alive) forever. 
\rtl2 After some time, Jesus has met a young man on the street, who has turned to Him with the words: ìSweet
teacher, can I ask you something?î Then Jesus has said ìTell me, what do you want to ask me?î And he has
answered: ìHow can I reach life forever?î 
\ln 79.06
\bt Then Isus says to him why you tell me that I am generous? Generous is only the God.
\anc mrk.10:18
\rtl2 Jesus has asked him: ìWhy do you name me sweet? You can name in that way only the God. Only the God
is sweet.î 
\co SH: RECRAFT?? - Generous to Good
\tst In your opinion what does it mean to be generous?
\tsta RC: To be good. (SH: Its the same as good?) Yes.
\tsta ER: It means a person who gives all of himself for others. "Blag", someone who gives many things. A
sweet, good person. (NP: Do you know such a person?) Yes, I know such people. (NP: What are they
like?) Good, generous ("blagi").
\tst Why do you think Jesus says "Generous is only the God." ?
\tsta RC: Maybe because on earth there arent any such clean... Maybe because God is the one who teaches
people about goodness and generousness (Blag) and he teaches them this goodness and hes the only one
who baptizes the sinners, while people here on earth arent like this.
\tsta ER: Because this man has asked for something from him, more accurately: he has asked how he can give
him eternal life, and Jesus answered that only God can do that. God has eternal life.
\ln 79.07
\bt After that He tells to him that the life will be inherited 
\anc mat.19:17
\rtl2 Then Jesus has said to this man that 
\tst What is the life that will be inherited... in your opinion?
\tsta RC: The truth is there isnt any such thing as eternal life, but when a person lives a good life and people
love him he will be a long time in their hearts. Thats it; that throughout all life people will leave but when
they follow Gods laws thru this they will stay forever. (SH: So there is no after life?) Maybe there is, I
dont know.
\tsta ER: I think that by eternal life is understood that as a person will be immortal; to never die and never
disappear from planet earth. But there are no such immortal people, at least not on our planet.
\ln 79.07.1
\bt if he keeps in the orders dont lie, dont steal, dont kill, respect your mother and your father.
\anc mrk.10:19
\rtl2 if you keep the rules in all your life donít to steal, donít to lie, donít to commit adultery, and if you keep
well with your mother and father, then you can get what do you want, in other words, life forever. 
\ln 79.08
\bt Then the man answers to Him that he knows these orders from his young years.
\anc mrk.10:20
\rtl1 And he says that he lives with the Godís rules from his young age, and that he doesnít steal, doesnít lie
from his young age. 
\rtl2 And the man has answered that he keep all that rules from his young age and that in the moment he is
rich. 
\co Does "know" imply "obey" too, like in the text?
\tst What does it mean that "he knows these orders from his youth"?
\tsta RC: That he lives that way. He follows Gods laws and he lives correctly, even from the time when he was
young as a child. Thats the way he was brought up and thats the way he lives. He doesnt sin.
\tsta ER: It means that he has come across these things before, and has learned them. Someone has told him
them, maybe his parents and family. So he's known it since he was a child, since he was young, because
somebody had told him. They have guided him, advised him not to do such things and to respect his
mother and father.
\tst Why do you think he has to follow these laws?
\tsta RC: As a child he was brought up this way. And a person who thinks this way will follow the laws without
even trying, because thats how he was raised and thats how his life is.
\tsta ER: Because if he doesn't keep them, that's very bad, very negative. Every reasonable person knows it's
very wrong to kill, to steal, to lie. These our things every person knows are very bad and shouldn't be
done.
\ln 79.09
\bt Isus likes him and tell to him that one isnt enough for him (NP: he lacks one thing) to get that
aim/ goal: to sell everything that he has and to give the money to poor people.
\anc mrk.10:21
\cn CONNOT: In view of his feeling for him, the negative opener is a surprise, and might be made
smoother, ‚ÄòBut, nonetheless, He said, ‚Äò¬†.¬†.¬†.¬†‚Äô 
\rtl1 But he is a rich man, and Jesus says to him that he has to sell all his riches and to give it to the poor
people. 
\rtl2 Then Jesus has said to him: ìIf you are rich, sell everything and that what will you win, give everything
to poor people.î 
\co SH: RECRAFT: Add "treasure in heaven" and "follow Me"?
\tst Why do you think all that the young man has done, isn't enough? 
\tsta RC: Because a person shouldnt want to have everything for himself. You have to think about others who
dont have. And this is the one thing he hadnt followed. He is extremely well off and he lives according
to Gods laws but the one thing he hasnt fulfilled is that there are poor people and he has to give to them
as well.
\tsta ER: Because he has to absolutely everything for it to be enough, in other words to continue all his life
until death to help, to give to people, do do only kind/ good things, in order to have eternal life. To have
eternal life after he dies, perhaps. 'Cause I understood that he wanted to live forever without dying,
but there's no way that can happen. Only Jesus rose from the dead.
\ln 79.10
\bt The man disappoints (NP: is disappointed) because he has been rich and disappoints (NP: felt
sad/ hurt), and goes.
\anc mrk.10:22
\rtl1 Then the rich man has become sad and went. 
\rtl2 Then the man has become sad and went. 
\ln 79.11
\bt Then Isus turns to his students and tells them that very difficult rich people will go into skys
kingdom (Gods kingdom)
\anc mrk.10:23
\rtl1 And Jesus has said
\rtl2 After that Jesus has arrived to his students. He has become to speak with them and he has turned to
them with the words: ìIt is difficult to the rich people to come in the Godís kingdom. 
\tst Where is this sky's kingdom do you think?
\tsta RC: In the sky/heaven, with God. 
\tsta ER: In the sky. In other words, on this earth, but in the sky.
\ln 79.12
\bt and it is easier camel goes during (NP: through) needle ears than the rich goes to the Gods
kingdom.
\anc mrk:10:25
\rtl1 that more easily the camel go during needleís ears than the rich man separate from his riches. 
\rtl2 It is so difficult as the camels can pass in needleís ears.î 
\co Backtranslator smiles, seemingly amused.
\co LM during onsite: Check on the exact meaning of the proverb in Jesus' time, and compare it to how it is
interpreted by the people here; "impossible" or just "very difficult"?
\tst If you had to use a Bulgarian proverb to say this, what is it? And what does it mean?
\tsta RC: (Sh: she couldnt think of any at the moment so I asked: What does this saying mean, a camel thru..?)
That its impossible. Bulgarian has such proverbs but I cant think of an exact one right now. But this one
is great.
\tsta ER: (laughing) A collegue of mine had made a mistake and this woman of about 30 years old therefore
had to pay a certain amount of money, but she said: "Even if Safinka climbs on top of the mosque, I
won't pay that money." In other words: it'll never happen. But there are others like that, for example: "a
fly turning into an elephant", in other words: it'll never happen.
\tst Why do you think Jesus say's it's very difficult for rich people to get to the sky's kingdom?
\tsta RC: Because the truth is they want to have everything. A lot of everything. And these kind of people
with great difficulty give to those who are left, to the poor, and those without anything. And they arent
righteous enough to go to Gods kingdom. Because they think more about themselves than those close to
them or the poor.
\tsta ER: I don't think it's exactly like that, becaus I think anybody could. This man, even though he is rich,
it's not compulsory for him to become poor to enter the sky's kingdom. It's enough for him to help poor
people and to give money to those who don't have as much in order to enter the sky's kingdom. Not to
become poor. Of course he'll help a lot of people if he sells everything at once and gives it to them, but
it's the same to help regularly, for example by giving every week or every month money, clothes,
medicine, food. That can help too. (NP: So why do you think Jesus said this?) Because apparently it
used to be that way back then, many years ago.
\ln 79.13
\bt Then students ask Him: And who can be saved?
\anc mrk.10:26
\rtl1 And then Peter has asked: ìWho can be saved?î 
\rtl2 Then Peter has said to Jesus: ìThen who can come in the Godís kingdom?î 
\tst Who needs to be saved from what, do you think?
\tsta RC:  From these sins, like greed, evil, lies. People need to be saved from these sins and these negative
qualities.
\tsta ER: I don't know. (NP plays it again and asks: What do they mean?) They mean, if the rich can't enter
the sky's kingdom, who can then? In other words: all the other people. That the poor and the semi-rich
can enter the sky's kingdom, but not the rich. But why shouldn't they enter if they regularly help other
people? (NP: So if it's not possible for the rich...) Then not at all for the poor. But maybe they're
allowed into the sky's kingdom because all their lives they've lived in poverty and misery all their lives.
NR: But life shows that the rich always win. ER: Rich people always win the battle when it's against a
poorer person.
\ln 79.14
\bt Isus answers them that for a man thats impossible. It is possible only for the God.
\anc mrk.10:27
\rtl1 And Jesus says only the God but the people canít.
\rtl2 Jesus said that it will be the best only the young children to come in the Godís kingdom. 
\ln 79.15
\bt Then Peter tells Him that they have left everything and have followed Him.
\anc mrk.10:28
\tst What do you think it means to follow Jesus?
\tsta RC: To do everything he tells them to do. To give everything to him, to his teaching, to his mission. And
to help him.
\tsta NR: To believe in him unconditionally. To listen to him, to respect him.
\tsta ER: To do just like he does with all people.
\ln 79.16
\bt And Isus replies that He tells the true that there isnt a man who has left brothers, sisters,
mother, father, home because for the sake of (NP: Him and) gentle/ good things
\anc mrk.10:29
\co blagovestie (gentle/ good things): old Bulgarian word - must be changed
\co NP: We skipped this part for the second testing, because we decided to cut it. It is too confusing.
\tst Do you understand this?
\tsta RC: No.
\tst For what reason are people supposed to leave these things?
\tsta RC: To leave brothers, sisters and home... so to follow Jesus isnt at all easy. Because he is fulfilling a
mission which is really difficult, to teach people about what is good. And because of that they have
reject these things in order to follow his. And they themselves have to work out this mission, to help
those who are poorer, the poor. They have to sacrifice themselves and their families in order to help
others.
\ln 79.17
\bt and not to receive a hundred times more brothers, sisters, mothers, fathers and a hundred times
more good things and together with it life forever.
\anc mrk.10:30
\co Backtranslator: bit about 100x more brothers etc. is confusing
\co Backtranslator: hardly understand the last sentence
\tst How can a person receive all of this do you think?
\tsta RC: Well the truth is it speaks of persecution. Because not everywhere will people receive their
teaching with good feelings. Some people will banish them. As for eternal life, what I said at the
beginning, its not about the person but the faith itself.

\co We might cut out the last bit seen as it is confusing.

\co I'm still working on the most efficient formatting for these files.  For now, the transcription of the
orally crafted story is broken up according to where Tomka broke it up during his backtranslation. 
Therefore, backtranslation 1 is lined up pretty tight (to the transcription).  However, KawÔre obviously
didnt break the story exactly like Tomka did during his backtranslation.  So I broke his backtranslation
up so that it would line up (as good as I could get it) with Tomka's backtranslation for comparison
reasons.  Having said that, I do think it would be profitable to see the transcription broken up
according to where KawÔre broke it up during his backtranslation.  Doing this would allow me to 'tightly'
line up his backtranslation with the transcription.  This would be good for langauge learning purposes.

see L&C entry espirito.

can go more generic but you can't go more specific. So you can't name the specific animals that God
made (lion, bear, etc) or the ones that went on the ark. Same here, if the Bible doesn't give specific
examples then we can't either.

\fix Scratch
\fix Basically we need to compile everything we know about Imere (if we're indeed going to use Imere in
the story set) and be deliberate about making sure the story set as a whole cover the unbiblical views
they have of him (ie. parents, being born/was created...)  Do they worship/respect Imere? Does he have
authority over other spirits?
\cn How much is a storyteller free to add when telling one of the bondo heritage stories.
\fix Keep an eye on line 14 in the Fall story.  It may have implications for the Spirit World portion of this
story.
\ln 01.26
\bt2 [In its entirety]  Ai o Deus e sozinho, ai Ele olhava pra cima via buraco no ceu, ai Ele pensava o que e
que eu vou fazer ai no ceu pra ocupar esse buraco. Dai Ele pensou fazer coisas pra ocupar aquele
buraco. 

Ai  primeiro Ele pensou: Ah vou fazer dia e noite, ai Ele fez dia e noite. Ai Ele pensou ai deu mais um
dia ai Ele pensou sera que so esses dois que eu vou fazer.

Ai Ele pensou eu vou fazer mais outros, terra, 

ai Ele parou, deu pause, sera que eu vou fazer so terra, terra ta bom? Ai Ele pensou vou fazer a agua, ai
Ele fez o mar, ai Ele tambem fez o divisao da terra. Divisao da terra e da agua. 

Ai deu no dia seguinte ai Ele pensou, que e que eu vou fazer, ai Ele pensou vou fazer uma coisa, vou
fazer o floresta, pra ficar na terra, 

ai Ele fez floresta, como caipim, como cipo, imbe. 

Ai deu mais um dia ai Ele pensou que e que vou fazer 

ai Ele pensou vou fazer o sol, lua, e as estrelas. 

E ai comecou a inventar, a fazer o sol, lua, estrela. Ai Ele deu mais um dia, depois que Ele fez sol,
estrela, e a lua, ai no dia seguinte, ai Ele pensou mais uma vez que e que eu vou fazer no pra ocupar a
agua 

ai Ele pensou fazer os bichos aquaticos como peixe, do aves,e jacare. 

Ai depois Ele pensou fazer outros bichos que andam na terra como queixada, onca, ai Ele fez esses
bichos 

ai depois Ele pensou fazer alguma alguem pra cuidar desse bicho ai Ele pensoui fazer homem ai Ele foi
pegou  pedaco de terra que e barro ai Ele comecou inventar fazer boneco comecou fazer pe, perna, 

joelho, braco, mao, orelha, nariz, boca, como se fosse humano, voce homen, ai Ele comecou fazer. 

Ai depois que Ele fez esse boneco ai Ele pensou sera que esse boneco vai andar assi? Nao, eu vou da um
vida pra ele, O Deus comecou a soprar no pelo nariz do boneco, ai Ele comecou a soprar soprar e depois
o boneco comecou a se movimentar ai Ele soprou de novo ai Ele respirou, soprou de novo e o homem
levantou o boneco se transformou em homem e se levantou, 

ai o Deus resolveu chamar todos aqueles bichos que Ele tinha transformado, chamou tudos primeiro. Ai
Ele chamou esses bichos so pra colocar o nome dele como Adao, 

ai chamarao ele como Adao, de Adao dizendo. Ai depois Ele chamou um monte de bicho ne, Ele chamou
os bichos so pra ser amigo desse Adao mais nenhum dos amigos dele mais ninguem combinou com ele. 

Ai Deus pensou, no que e que eu vou fazer quem e que vai ser companheiro desse homem ai Deus pensou
ne, ah Eu vou fazer Adao dormir ai entao Adao deitou e dormiu bem, bem muito mesmo ai e como Adao
tinha dormido bem profundo. 

Ai Deus foi la tirou costela dele, ai fez, tirou, cortou pedaco de costela, nao sei como Ele transformou
pedaco de costela em mulher, 

ai Adao acordou e viu essa mulher, ue da onde essa mulher veio, ai entao Adao falou agora eu vou me
casar com essa mulher, com ela que eu vou trabalhar nos vamos cuidar junto desses matos, bichos, aguas,
assim o Deus fez mulher pra Adao. 

Ai Deus ficou animado feliz com aqueles bichos que Ele tinha inventado, ai Ele falou quem que vai me
ajudar, ai entao Ele pensou eu vou fazer alguem pra me ajudar, ai Ele fez. 

Ai tudo, tudo aqueles que Deus fazia inventava Ele ficava feliz. Por causa deles ne Ele ficava feliz
aqueles bichos tambem gostava deles, tinha um representante daqueles bichos falou: ah, mentira desse
cara, mentira desse Deus, Ele quer ser dependente, Ele quer ficar deitado e agente fazendo coisa pra
Ele, disse esse representante dos bichos.

Ai um que era representante tava foi la pra os bichos falando que o Deus tava mentindo pra eles. Foi
assim outros bichos gostava de Deus mais um que era poderoso que nao gostava de Deus, ai o Deus tinha
escutado a fala do bicho que tinha falado mal Dele. 

Agora voces vao num lugar. Um lugar onde tem fogo que nao acaba, vao pra onde tem frio que nao
acaba, e a historia acabou assim.

\cn There's still a big question about what would be best to use for God.  When they hear 'Deus' they
immediately think of Imere.  The testing shows some differences between Imere and the God of the
Bible.  For example, he didn't always exist, he has a mom and dad (I think - and I think he killed his dad
too), and there are also some differences regarding things he created.  However, there are some basic
similarities as well...regarding things they created, the fact that he gives punishment, etc...  Ante
backtranslated Mactampo's telling of their Imere story.  This will be helpful in gathering more info
about their concept of Imere.  Also, in the recording of the testing session with Oiope, Ante recounted
(in Portuguese) some of the Imere story.  This was natural because this first story raises some
immediate barriers...not necessarily ngegative...just conflicting concepts between the God of the Bible
and Imere...which will be an inevitable issue if we stick with Imere as the key term for God.  1.01.35 -
1.10.15...here we had an interesting discussion regarding the 'just' nature of Imere.  For now, it seems
to me that their concept of Imere's character carries an attribute of justness.  He doesn't give
punishment to be mean, he gives punishment when it is deserved.

\cn The whole spirit world thing still seems a little gray to me...even when I tell it in English, so it's no
surprise that anchoring this section of the story is a challenge.  Honestly, from what we're giving him
(as far as sources go) he seems to be getting the idea of what's going on fairly well (conceptually). 
What's difficult, obviously, is putting a nice Bible verse next to each idea...which like I alluded to
earlier, is not necessarily easy even in English.  I did think our crafter had a good idea and he did it in
this revision.  He noticed that the spirits praised God when God was making things SO he wanted to put
their creation before the creation of the world.  He kept what happened to them at the end of the story
because to him it seemed like 'everyone was on board' during the creative process.  Made sense to me! 
I'm glad you're the consultant (ha).

\co I'm still working on the most efficient formatting for these files.  For now, the transcription of the
orally crafted story is broken up according to where Tomka broke it up during his backtranslation. 
Therefore, backtranslation 1 is lined up pretty tight (to the transcription).  However, KawÔre obviously
didnt break the story exactly like Tomka did during his backtranslation.  So I broke his backtranslation
up so that it would line up (as good as I could get it) with Tomka's backtranslation for comparison
reasons.  Having said that, I do think it would be profitable to see the transcription broken up
according to where KawÔre broke it up during his backtranslation.  Doing this would allow me to 'tightly'
line up his backtranslation with the transcription.  This would be good for langauge learning purposes.

\fix He made the only sense out of it that he could, that the snake was just a snake, so Eve's descendants
couldn't kill the snake himself, it would have to be the snake's descendants. A couple of things you could
do to help with this: 1) Say that the snake is Satan and anchor it with rev 12:9. 2) Say in the Spirit
world story that Satan tries to trick people and then make sure they use the same verb in this story when
Eve says "the snake tricked me". 3) Just make sure it's right in this story, and even if they don't
initially make the connection (like this guy) keep checking for it until they do....without you giving it
away of course. 
\fix Assuming option 3 gets eliminated, try option 2 next...which would have implications for the first
story.  Option 1 is a last resort to make sure they are understanding that the snake is actually the chefe
dos espiritos maus, but it is acceptable

\anc Gen.03.16, Translator's Handbook says, I will greatly multiply your pain in childbearing: this
is not in the form of a curse, as in the case of the snake, although the content has the effect
of a curse. Greatly multiply translates a Hebrew intensive construction: ‚ÄúI will very much
increase, make worse your pain.‚Äù Pain translates a word meaning ‚Äútrouble, difficulty, labor.‚Äù
Childbearing is literally ‚Äúconception.‚Äù The focus is not upon the act of conception but rather
upon the state of pregnancy, and so FRCL has ‚ÄúI will make your pregnancies painful,‚Äù and
TEV ‚Äú‚Ä¶increase your trouble in pregnancy.‚Äù
\ret Dai Ele deu castigo para a Eva: - Eva no momento que vocÍ ficar gestante as dores v„o te pegar, durante a
gravidez vocÍ vai sentir dores atÈ ganhar o seu primeiro filho.

\ln 03b.06
\tra oretput keruwongne txinano  imo  eram  keni  imere wok  ii man ,kalotxin  keni imonmo  man imere  alo

\bt Quando eles se dividiram e outros que foram por outro lado estavam com o Deus de verdade e o

\eng When they divided and the others who went to the other side were with the true God and the

\anc How would you approach this?
\cn Okay.  At times, I get concerned about how certain things aren't easily anchorable.  However, I'm
having to balance a few things in my mind (I'm asking for counsel here).  1.  These guys know nothing
about the Bible, they have no Scripture portions, and this is the first time they've heard any of this  2. 
I find myself continually asking, 'What is it that we're trying to communicate?'  So if there's not a
major theological or content discrepency, I'm finding myself to have more lenient tendencies than I did
before we started this process (just being honest).  3.  We're talking about conveying a panorama of
Redemptive History in 12-15 stories here, so it's impossible for us not to expect them to try and make
sense of some of the gaps in their own minds...in a way that's in keeping with their own storytelling
methods.

So my question...for instance, in the last two lines are we able to find nice anchors for this idea? 
Despite whether the answer is yes or no, isn't this essentially what we're trying to communicate when
we jump from the Fall to Elijah?  That essentially people went in one of two different
directions...following the One True God or that they began embracing false gods.  Feel free to rebuke
me (ha)!  I guess essentially I'm struggling with how much time to invest in correcting 'non-essentials'
that really don't affect the central message...and how much should I depend on the forthcoming written
translation to fill 'knowledge gaps' and to eventually provide a fuller understanding of the big picture?

\dt 28/Sep/2009

\c H-00
\t Hunsrik Exploratory Panorama Set Overview
\stg Bkgrnd (Hunsrik)
\co Hunsrik
\co Reason: Daniel and Stan see the following possibilities for redemptive themes among the Hunsrik:
Grace, Relationship, Forgiveness, Mediator, Messiah. We're leaning heavily to the Relationship and
Mediator themes initially. The other themes listed above will probably still apear as currents through the
exploratory panorama though they may not be fully developed in terms of Problem, Prediction, Jesus as
the Solution and Response.
\co We'll expand these descriptions in the days and weeks to come.
\co Story crafter's name or initials
\co Backtranslator's name or initials

\bld Story 1 -- Creation of the Spirit World
\co We're looking at separating the two creation stories based on length of telling. Consistently, all of our
house churches have asked questions about this and othe raspects of cosmology.
\cn God - creator of heaven

\bld Story 2 -- Creation of the Physical World
\co This story is the foundaiton for all we know about the relationship that God desires to have with man.
Also relavent to our people is the basis of the relationship between a husband and wife.
\cn God - creator of earth, Holy Spirit

\bld Story 3 -- The Fall of Mankind
\co This story shows the entrance of a need for a mediator between God and man and the broken
relationship between God and man. This story is actually the one that introduces the problem related to
relationship and mediator. We see here the seed form of the prediction of the Messiah.

\bld Story 4 -- Covenant with Israel & 10 Commandments
\co This story shows God entering into a relationship with Israel in order to have a relationship with the
other nations. Israel becomes a nation-priest, a mediating nation, between God and the other nations.
The 10 Commandments will provide a corrective to the Catholic catechism exclusion of having no
"graven images."

\bld Story 5 -- Golden Calf
\co  This story shows Moses as mediator between God and Israel. This story also addresses the issue of
idolatry, praying to the saints, among our people.

\bld Story 6 -- David and Bathsheba w/ Nathan and David
\co This story shows broken relationships on many levels of society and with God. Nathan's visit may be
incuded with this story as well. God sends a prophet who is something as a  mediator.

\bld Story 7 -- Nathan and David w/ Death of the Child and Psalm 51
\co This story will either start with Nathan's visit or the death of the child, depending on how the previous
story is crafted. We believe the Psalm is vital to show repentence. This story will address the idea of
original sin that we discovered in Porto Velho about mother's milk passing sin to the child.
\cn Forgiveness of sins

\cn It appears that we have left out the "prediction" story, aside from the story of the Fall which is very
general. We are now aware of this possible gap and will be considering stories to use for this purpose.
We'll let you know when we decide a story that meets this need in the story set.

\bld Story 8 -- The Birth of Jesus
\co You can't have a redemptive set without this story. There's no way to understand Jesus without his
birth. We may also use this in some way to counter the original sin issue and mother's milk. We'll see.
\cn Jesus the Son, the Holy Spirit, born of the virgin Mary and forgiveness of sins

\bld Story 9 -- John the Baptist and Jesus' Baptism
\co John's proclamation was repentence for forgiveness of sin - restoration of relationship, and making
straight the path for the Messiah. Jesus' baptism deals with one aspect of the baptism barrier we face
among our people.

\bld Story 10 -- Parable of the Unjust Servant
\co This story deals with relationship and forgiveness. It is one that has struck a bell with our people in
past studies.

\bld Story 11 -- Parable of the Wedding Feast
\co This story deals with relationship, heaven, and forgiveness.

\bld Story 12 -- Parable of the Prodigal Son
\co This story deals with relationship and forgiveness. It also has struck a bell with our people in the past.
Here we see God as Father.
\cn God the Father

\bld Story 13 -- Crucifixion
\co This story shows Jesus as mediator and the one who pays the price to restore the relationship that God
desires to have with us. This one will probably end up being 2-3 stories in order to show the arrest/trial
and crucifixion.
\cn suffered under Pilate, crucified, died and buried

\bld Story 14 -- Resurrection
\co Without this there is no Christianity, regardless of theme choice.
\cn Raised on the third day and ascended into heaven and seated at the right hand of the Father

\bld Story 15 -- Peter's Proclamation (Acts 2)
\co This story may be used in conjunction with Acts 1 in two stories. This will introduce the holy spirit, the
church, and the Lord's supper and baptism after repentence.
\cn Jesus is Lord, church, communion of the saints

\cn After a once-over from the Creed, it seems we need to have a clearer picture of the bodily resurrection
from the dead and the return of Christ to judge the living and the dead. We'll be looking more closely at
these possible gaps in the exploratory set.

\cn Below is where we will expand the exploratory set for our overall, longer set.
\co Story 1 -- Creation of the Spirit World
\co Story 2 -- Creation of the Physical World
\co Story 3 -- The Fall of Mankind
\dt 28/Sep/2009

que Deus proibiu o homen comer desta fruta? A: Dar escolha. Porque Deus ia criar desta ·rvore? A:  O
mesmo. Dar a eles escolha.
\anc Gen.03:15-17
\cn 2nd time through the Tree of Knowledge was corrected. Culture: The fact that God planned for Adam to
care for the land and plant crops is important to this agriculturally-based society. This was shown by
how easily the command given to Adam to care for the Garden of Eden was picked up during testing.
Today, the government's enviromental agencies as well as private ones are making agricultural life
difficult. The are more incentives for people to return their lands to forest than to plant them with
crops. The larger Urban culture, among the more educated, do not value the agricultral industry and
view it as destroying the nature beauty. However this passage is useful in combating an unbiblical view
that the elite, in many Western nations are touting.

young man had time to answer. Showing he had reason to be somewhat tentative???? Hmmmm.

\tst1 Q: O que sigifica o homen e a mulher se tornam um sÛ carne? A: Deficil.... He is a single guy and
probably answered this question correctly....Also, may have been intimidated with the ladies present.
\anc Gen.03:24
\cn Today, the younger generations of the Hunsrik and even some older are not respectful of the bond that
God intends between a man and woman. While Catholics do not officially receive divorces many of
them live separated form their husbands and wives but with another partner creating children outside
the bonds of marriage. They prefer this and accept it over leaving the Catholic Church. The government
grants divorce but most do not seek it because they still recognize the authority of the Catholic Church
in regard to marriage. Younger Hunsrik most often live together for 5-10 years before officially
marrying in the Catholic Church. This in hopes of avoiding an official separation.

\ln 05.14
\bt1 Eles eram n˙s e n„o tinham vergonha. 
\bt2 Os dois estavam n˙s mas n„o se envergonhavam um do outro. 
\eng The two were nude but they were not ashamed of each other.
\tst1 Q: Por que o homen e a mulher n„o tinham vergonha para estar nu? A: Pura, pureza. Depois comeram a
fruta e envergonhou.
\anc Gen.03:25
\cn Among the Hunsrik this is significant because their tranditional view of marital relations is that it is
based in sin, i.e. marital, 'sexual', relations are sinful. In Hunsrik the word for 'sexual relations'
literally translates into English as 'the bads.' This comes from their understanding of their Catholic
heritage which teaches that 'sex' is sinful. A generation or two ago brides would be given a nuptial lace
clothe that was to cover or veil the brides entire body on her wedding night so as to cover her 'shame.'
The only opening was over the genital area. While this view is changing today among secularizing
forces it still remains an important aspect of culture and needs to be dealt with. Among the older
generation this view is quite strong still and any public display of affection is viewed with disdain.
Naturally in our Brazilian Latin American context where public display of affection is demonstrated, if
not outright flaunted, their is a conflict between cultural worldviews. Dealing with this also will set the
stage for showing that it is not sinful for those called to ministry to marry.

\cn This word 'ferxproch' is the word for promised. When it is used it is as good as done. This was the
undoubtedly the word the Hunsrik used when contracts were oral and not written. They explained that it
is used not only in engagement but also when dealing with good or animals, land, etc. Their
understanding was right on here.

\cn This was the most problematic area that I encountered. The story specifically states that the men from
the East went and worshipped the baby Jesus. Those tested automatically viewed the visit as involving
the worship of Mary. One person spoke up but no one disputed what was said. Definitely confirming
what we have found and that is...The worship of Mary is key to breaking Folk Catholicism.

they brought grifts and not needed for clearer understanding. So, no fix was necesaary.

\ln 201.21

and your son."
\cn In this story I think that the way that Matthew was led by the Holy Spirit to address Jesus and Mary as
'the boy and his mother' is important. The angel stated it in this manner both times he appeared to
Joseph. I am thinking that this will need to be changed here when Joseph is told to return to Israel and
above when he is told to take 'the boy and his mother' and flee to Egypt. Our crafter used 'family' the
first time and the second 'your wife and child' the second. If Matthew refered two times in the same
manner I think, especially in our Catholic and ever growing secular context that this is highly important
because it places the child Jesus before his mother and does not refer to Joseph as the father. Yet,
leaves him with the responsibility of caring for them. It appears to be done in this manner to reiterate
the miraculous birth.

repent of your sins.  Q:When should a person be baptized?  A: When he has a mind to understand. Being
baptized as a child does nothing. You must be an adult.
\anc mat.03:13
\cn The issue of baptism, i.e. infant baptism, is huge in the Hunsrik culture. They are taught that without
baptism of the baby salvation is not possible. While more and more fall away from this it is often
difficult for parents to stand against the culture when grandparents and other family members
pressure. But this knowledge is a BIG first step. We will be including many stories showing adult
baptism.

\eng John, the Baptist, didn't want to do it.

\eng He believed that he needed to be baptised by Jesus and that he shouldn't baptise Jesus.

Jo„o ouviu

\bt Os professores da religi√£o (das leis) e o chefe dos sacerdotes procurarem um plano para matar
Jesus mas tinham medo de fazer isto porque tinha muitas pessoas por perto. 
\eng The teachers of religion (the laws) and the cheifs of the priests were looking for a plan to kill
Jesus but they were afraid to do this because he had many people around him.
\tst1 Q: What do you think? Why did the religious leaders adn the high priest become afraid of the people
when they were near them? A:Because they knew that the people believed in Jesus as the Christ ...
\anc luk.22:02
\ln 290.03
\bt Da√≠ o Diabo entrou em Judas Iscariotes que era um dos doze ap√≥stolos de Jesus.
\eng Then the Devil entered into Judas Iscariot who was one of the 12 apostles of Jesus.
\tst1 Q: What is the significance....'the Devil went into Judas Iscariot?"  A: Judas let the Devil enter him.
He was a person who wanted money and power. His love was for money.  Q: Today, can the Devil got
into other people? A: Yes he can. Into anyone. 
\anc luk.22:03
\cn Demon possession is a part of the culture. They have the EVIL EYE and various other supersticians as
well. However, the Hunsrik are secularizing so it is not uncommon to find individuals scoffing at demon
possession. The back translator of this story thought I should leave the possession part of the story out
because she did not like it implying that she has her doubts about it. Adding other stories of demons and
also the Devil will be important in the future. 
\ln 290.04
\bt  Judas foi falar com o chefes dos soldados do templo para entregar Jesus nas m√£os deles. 
\eng Judas went to talk with the cheif of the soldiers of the temple to bring Jesus into their hands
\anc luk.22:04
\ln 290.05
\bt O Chefe dos sacerdotes e os professores das leis de religi√£o ficarem felizes com este atitude de
Judas e prometerem 30 moedas de prata se ele fizesse isso. 
\eng The Chief of the priests and the teachers of religious law were happy with this attitude of
Judas and promised him 30 coins of silver if he did this.
\tst1 Q: Why were the priest and the religious leaders happy at what Judas did? A: They were afraid of
losing their authority to rule and hence their power.
\anc luk.22:05, Mat.26:15
\ln 290.06
\bt Ent√£o Judas procurou um meio para trair Jesus quando o povo n√£o tivesse junto com dele.   
\eng So Judas looked for a chance to betray Jesus when the people were not near him.

\anc luk.22:19
\cn The Lord's Supper for most means anything but a remembrance. The back translator shared that, in her
understanding, the Lord's Supper is GRACE (Consistent with Catholic teaching). She separates
FORGIVENESS though saying that forgiveness comes at the beginning of the mass and then grace at
the end when the cracker dipped in the wine is eatten. I have never looked at grace and forgiveness as
totally separate. Certainly, stories where grace is demonstrated to individuals or groups of individuals
will be important. Especially those that focus upon heart rather than ritual. This should be both in the
OT and NT because the Catholic ritual system is very OT in many ways.
\ln 292.06
\bt Depois do jantar Jesus pegou o c√°lice com vinho e disse, ‚ÄúEssa √© a nova alian√ßa que ser√° feito

\eng After dinner Jesus got the cup with wine and said, "This is a new alliance that will be made
between God and his people that is confirmed with my blood which is pour for you.
\tst1 Q: What is the significance of "the new covenant?" A: From this point on....I poured out my blood for
your sins.
\anc luk.22:20
\ln 292.07
\bt Vejam, est√° aqui am mesa aquele que vai me entregar. O Filho do Homen vai morrer como Deus
j√° deixou preparado. E ai daquele que fizer isto.‚Äù 
\eng See, this one here is the same one who will turn me in. The Son of Man will die just as God has
prepared. And there from he who does this."

be accomplished....to die on the cross for sinners.... pecadores...

\c K-00
\t K'bou Story Set, etc.
\stg Bkgrnd (K'bou)
\co <Redemptive theme> Trusting God vs. Trusting Self  Trusting God for all things, including our salvation.
[Subpoints: God's Plan of Salvation, Jesus is Lord; (Master/Submission)]
\co <Purpose> To help the K'bou see salvation is the completed work of God and they need to trust (and obey)
the Way He already made. To help the K'bou see that following after money is a trap of Satan to keep
them from following God.
\co <Background> Jacob exemplifies the mentality of being too self oriented and too busy for God that the
Kb culture seems to exhibit. We hope that once we are able to make the story clear enough, that people
will be interested in this character that gets the best of others (they love that in their fables.) They
have a typical Muslim worldview; they believe in One God to whom they are slaves; salvation is earned
by good works - they hope.  Lying is a way of life, so K'bou are not trust-worthy and don't trust each
other. They don't trust God to meet their needs; they think success must be their own doing. Money
dominates their WHOLE THINKING and worldview. They all try to take advantage of each other and to
avoid being taken advantage of by others.
\co <Basic Biblical concepts>  God is the Supreme Authority and expects our obedience. God is completely
trust-worthy; man is seldom trustworthy. God is always trying to get man to trust Him. Jacob wouldn't
submit to God, so God had to break him of his self-sufficiency.  God expects us to trust Him rather than
manipulate situations for our own benefit.  God is always true to His word; His sovereign plan for our
salvation will be fulfilled.
\co <Cohesion>  The Blessings of God are many and manifold, but ultimately, they are fulfilled in Christ. 
God is seeking out man.
\co <Other thoughts>  God's plan included blessing the world (incl. Kbs) through Abraham's descendents, so
God promised to bless Jacob. Jacob lived without feeling blessed by God's Blessing.  K'bou are too hard
at work trying to "bless" themselves, to know God's blessing. We feel God's blessing when we are in
close relationship to Him. Complete Blessing of God found in Christ. 

\old <Back Translation> We recorded the story on a cassette tape and had the BT listen twice
and then he gave a bt sentence by sentence as we recorded the process on another
recorder. Then I typed out what the BT said in French and from that, translated it to
English. 
\co <Back Translation> We record the story in an audio file and play it off the computer. The BT listens
twice - or more. The translation is then made sentence by sentence with the translation being written
down. It was much too confusing to transcript a recording that went back and forth on sentence
comprehension and then knowing whether sentences were repeated or only said once in the original.
The level of French is generally not good enough to get a faithful translation on any sentences that go
"outside their box." From the written French translation, I translate it into English.
\co <List of potential stories> Please see the Excel file we made for this purpose
\co <Resources for crafting> Almost nothing for Kanembou. We got some script preparation videos. We
have a set of pictures on our computer, but we haven't found them that helpful. Life here is about like
life in Jesus's day, so there is less need for cultural pictures. Story boarding seems to help the most.
There is no Bible translated in K'bou. Some stories (Bible passages) have been translated by a former
missionary, but he did not do Jacob. The FranÁais Courant Bible (French easy language Bible).

\old <Two testing groups> For our first story, we just asked two people to answer our testing
questions; one is a younger man, with a little primary school education; and one is a
middle-aged woman who hasn't attended school. We don't know if they will be available for
future testing.
\co <Two testing groups> MHW has some friends he wants us to test with. Have to find another group too.
We'll have to tell about them before each story.
\old <Crafter> Our Crafter, "Aboriginal," is a middle-aged man who has not had much schooling.
He has taught himself oral French but his level is not too high. He loves to laugh and seems
to like to tell stories informally. 
\co <Crafter> Our main crafter now, MHW, is a young man in his 20s. He has been extremely faithful to
come help us. He is even willing to help us without pay (which is a work of God, although we do give him
some help every week -about $10 - so that he doesn't have to leave us to find a job in order to be able to
eat.)
\old <Back Translator> "Abdellahi" is a high school student probably in his early twenties. His
French level is not that great, but probably typical of what we will find here. There are men,
who have better levels, but we are still looking for someone better. (Since our helpers may
change from story to story for now, we would rather give this information in the top lines of
each story.) 
\co <Back Translator> We have had a string of them. We will let you know story by story.

\dt 28/Sep/2009

\c K-07
\t Abraham Chosen
\stg Expl. (K'bou) JH
\co Language: K'bou
\co Reason for having this story in the set: Set lineage for Jacob; Abraham is example of someone learning
to trust God; He learned it to the point of entrusting the life of the son of the promise , his only son, 
into God's hands.
\co Crafter: MHW 5 Sept 09
\co Backtranslator: SMA 7 Sept 09
\co Resources used in crafting this story: the story (in French) that we crafted first, some Bible passages
(they are very spread out for this story) in French.
\co Test 1: (Name of person tested and date; How did they do retelling the story; any other comments)
\co Test 2: (Name of person tested and date; How did they do retelling the story; any other comments)

\ln 07.01
\bt Cette histoire, c'est l'histoire de Dieu, extraite de la Torah.
\bteng This story is the story of God, taken from the Torah.

\ln 07.02
\bt AprËs la mort d'Adam et Hawa, beaucoup de gens sont nÈs. Tous les gens nÈs sont pervers et la

\anc gen.06:08  gen.07:13  gen.08:16 gen.08:17

\cn We keep saying "the prophet Name" because M. respect uses "Nebi Name" for the title.

pour tous les gens.

change of heart. 
\rev This sentence is not expressing the thought well.

\bteng So the one who shows you mercy, I will show him mercy and the one who curses you, I will

\ln 07.10

\anc gen.13:03 gen.15.02

\ln 07.15
\bt Il a son Èpouse Zara, le prophËte Abraham. Zara n'a jamais accouchÈ.
\bteng He has his wife, Zarah, the prophet Abraham. Zarah has never given birth.
\anc gen.16.01
\ln 07.16
\bt Zara dit: "Prends notre servante et couche avec elle; peut-Ítre on trouvera un enfant."
\bteng Zarah said: "Take our servant girl and sleep with her; maybe we will have a child."
\anc gen.16.02
\tst Should Zarah have suggested that Abraham sleep with her slave girl? Why or why not?
\tst Do you think she got this idea from God or from the culture around her?
\ln 07.17
\bt Abraham couche avec la servante, un enfant est donc nÈ. Cet enfant est nommÈ IsmaÎl. 
\bteng Abraham slept with the servant girl, and so a child was born. This child is called Ishmael.
\anc gen.16.02 gen.16.15
\ln 07.18
\bt Dieu dit ‡ Abraham: "IsmaÎl aussi, sa famille va devenir nombreuse. ProphËte Abraham, moi et toi,
pour notre alliance sans fin, ce n'est pas envers IsmaÎl, cel‡ parvient. plutÙt entre l'enfant que toi
et Zara, vous mettrez au monde,que cel‡ parvient," Dieu dit ‡ Abraham.
\bteng God said to Abraham: "Ishmael also, his family will become numerous. Prophet Abraham, me
and you, for our alliance without end, it isn't with Ishmael that it will come, rather with the child
that you and Zarah will give birth to, that it will come." God said it to Abraham.
\anc gen.17.19 gen.17:20 gen.17:21 
\cn "alliance without end" is how we rendered "eternal covenant or agreement"
\tst Why was it important to God to choose the son of Abraham's legitimate wife instead of the
son of a concubine?
\ln 07.19
\bt Zarah, agÈe de 90 ans, et le prophËte Abraham ‡ 100 ans, ils ont mis un enfant au monde et cet
enfant Ètait nommÈ Isaak. C'est vraiment Ètonnant pour celui qui met au monde ‡ 100 ans. 
\bteng Zarah, aged 90, and the prophet Abraham, aged 100, they had a child and this child was named
Isaac. It is very amazing for someone to have a child at 100 years of age.
\anc gen.17:17  gen.21:05 gen.21:03 
\tst How are God's plans different than what men plan? Why does God do things that men do
not expect (are surprising)?
\ln 07.20
\bt L'enfant que Zara a mis au monde, Isaak, au jour de son sevrage, IsmaÎl a tacquinÈ [embÍtÈ - RH]
le petit enfant. 
\bteng The child that Zarah gave birth to, Isaac, on the day he was weaned, Ishmael aggravated the
little child.
\anc gen.21:08 gen.21:09 
\ln 07.21
\bt Zara dit, "L'enfant de notre servante dÈrange mon enfant. Et moi je n'aime pas cel‡, car je ne
veux pas qu'ils prennent ton hÈritage; chasse-les!"
\bteng Zarah said: "The child of our servant girl is bothering my child. And I don't like that, because I
don't want them to take your heritage; send them away!"
\anc gen.21:10 
\tst Zarah was the originator of the plan to have Ishmael, so why does she now not want
Ishmael to inherit with her son, Isaak? 
\tst Would you say that Zarah's reaction was too extreme? Why/ Why not?
\ln 07.22
\bt Donc le prophËte Abraham n'aime pas cette parole. Mais Dieu dit ‡ Abraham d'accepter ce que
dit Zara, "...Car notre alliance entre toi et moi provient chez Isaak et non chez IsmaÎl."
\bteng Well, the prophet Abraham doesn't like that word. But God told Abraham to accept what Zarah

\anc gen.21:11 gen.21:12

make alliances with people today?
\ln 07.23
\bt Alors des l'aube, il a donnÈ aux gens un peu de nourriture et il les a encouragÈ ‡ partir  [lit.- ils
les a renvoyÈ et ils sont partis - RH]. 
\bteng So at dawn, he gave the people [them - RH] a little food and he sent them away and they left.
\anc gen.21:14 
\ln 07.24
\bt Alors, plusieurs annÈes sont passÈes. Un jour Dieu lui dit, "L'enfant que tu aimes, c'est Isaak,

\bteng So many years passed. One day God told him: "The child you love, it's Isaac, take him and bring

\anc gen.22.02
\tst Why did God want Abraham to sacrifice/kill his son? 
\ln 07.25a
\bt Il aimait beaucoup son fils; mais il n'a pas laissÈ la parole de Dieu. ¿ cause de cel‡, il a amenÈ son
fils ‡ l'endroit ou` Dieu lui a montrÈ... 
\bteng He loved his son very much, but he didn't disobey [leave] God's word. Because of this, he

\ln 07.25b

m'aimes plus que ton enfant." 
\bteng ... he tied him up and just as he was about to kill him, God said: "Stop, because I know that you
love me more than your child."
\anc gen.22:09 gen.22:10 gen.22:12

\ln 07.26
\bt Il s'est arrÍtÈ; et il regarde derriËre lui et a trouvÈ dans les herbes un bÈlier qu'il a attrappÈ et a
ÈgorgÈ et a offert ‡ Dieu comme sacrifice ‡ la place de son fils. 
\bteng He stopped and looked behind himself and he found in the grass a ram which he caught, killed

\anc gen.22:13

\ln 07.27
\bt Dieu dit,"C'est moi qui te dit,"Toi, tu n'as pas transgressÈ [sautÈ=dÈsobÈir - RM] ma parole et gr‚ce
‡ [par - RH] toi, tout le peuple du monde aura la misÈricorde de Dieu, car toi tu n'as pas mÈprisÈ
[ignorÈ - RH] ma parole. 
\bteng God said: "It is I that tell you, 'You, you haven't jumped over my word (disobeyed Me), and

\anc gen.22:16 gen.22:18

\bteng And this is a story from God.

\gtst Was there anything surprising or strange in this story?  (If so, tell more about it.)
\gtstid Ada yang mengejutkan atau heran di kisah ini? (Kalau ada, ceritakanlah tentang itu.)
\ansid 1 - Tidak.
\ans 1 - No.
\ansid 2 - Tidak.
\ans 2 - No.
\ansid 3 - Tidak. Biaso bae.
\ans 3 - No. Just usual.
\gtst Was there anything you particularly liked or disliked about this story? Or something that made an
impression on you?  (If so, tell more about it.)
\gtstid Ada yang khususnya disukai atau tidak disukai tentang kisah ini?  Atau sesuatu yang mengesankan
(Kalau ada, ceritakanlah tentang itu.)
\ansid 1 - Semua bagus.
\ans 1 - All is good.
\ansid 2 - Tidak pakai baju.
\ans 2 - Not wearing clothes.
\ansid 3 - Semua bagus bae.
\ans 3 - All is just good.
\gtst Does this remind you of a story or event that you've heard from your own cultural context?  (If so, tell
more about it.)
\gtstid Apakah ini memperingatkan tentang kisah atau peristiwa yang didengar dari budaya Babak/Ibu
sendiri? (Kalau ada, ceritakanlah tentang itu.)
\ansid 1 - Tidak ada.
\ans 1 - There is none.
\ansid 2 - Pertama kali dengar.
\ans 2 - Heard for the first time.
\ansid 3 - Si Pahit Lidah.
\ans 3 - Si Pahit Lidah = The Bitter Tongue: A local fable figure; see Lo'am Cultural Stories
\gtst What do you think is the point of this story?  
\gtstid Apa topik kasih ini menurut Bapak/Ibu?
\ansid 1 - Tuhan menciptakan manusia dari tanah. Selanjutnya tidak dari tanah.
\ans 1 - God created the human from the earth. Afther that not from the earth anymore.
\ansid 2 - Nabi (Adam).
\ans 2 - The prophet, i.e. Nabi Adam.
\ansid 3 - Sebagai pasang-pasangan, lanang-betino.
\ans 3 - As partners, man-woman.
\gtst Who is the hero or villain in the story?
\gtstid Siapakah pahlawan (yang baik) atau siapakah penjahat (yang jahat) di kisah ini?
\ansid 1 - Tidak ada.
\ans 1 - There is none.
\ansid 2 - Tidak ada.
\ans 2 - There is none.
\ansid 3 - Dak katek.
\ans 3 - There is none.
\gtst Does this story seem like it could have actually happened (is true), or does it seem far-fetched (untrue)
or like a fable?  Why do you think this?
\gtstid Apakah kisah ini tampaknya sungguh-sungguh terjadi (kisah benar), atau tampaknya tidak menyakinkan
(kisah tak benar) atau tampaknya seperti dongeng? Mengapa?
\ansid 1 - Sungguh-sungguh.
\ans 1 - Seriously.
\ansid 2 - Termasuk dongeng. Kurang tahu.
\ans 2 - Belongs to fables. I do not really know.
\ansid 3 - Sungguh-sungguh.
\ans 3 - Seriously.

\ln 01.01

seeds did not grow (sprout) yet,

\ind Kemudian diambillah rusuk manusia itu dan dagingnya.

\ln 01.19
\nat Sesudah diembeknyo rusuk itu, ditutupnyo tempat diembek rusuk dari tu dengan dagingnyo.

\en After it was taken (by him) that rib, it was closed (by him the place) that rib (was taken from)
with flesh.
\anc gen.02:21

\ansid 1 - Pertanyaan yang aneh.
\ans 1 - That's a strange question.
\ans 2 - (Not asked.)
\ans 3 - (Not asked.)

\ln 01.20

\tst

\tst

\ln 01.22

\ind "Tulang dari tulang saya, daging dari daging saya."
\en "(So, this is her.) Bone from my bone. Flesh from my flesh."
\anc gen.02:23
\tst Why do you think did that human say "bone from my bone" and "flesh from my flesh"?
\ansid 1 - Karena dia tahu.
\ans 1 - Because he knows.
\ansplm 2 - Dio dari lanang.
\ans 2 - She's from the man.
\ansplm 3 - Dio ngerti bahwa betino dari dio.
\ans 3 - He anderstands that the woman is from himself.

\ln 01.23
\nat ---
\ind ---
\en ---
\old "Aku namoke dio betino, karno dio tu dari lanang."
\oldid "Saya bernama dia perempuan, karena dia dari laki-laki."
\olden "I {have the} name her women, because she is from the man."

\ln 02.01

taman ini dak boleh kau makan, kan?"
\bt Na, ular ini mengajak perampuan ini berbicara. Kata ular ini kepada perampuan ini: "Bukannya
semua buah yang ada di taman ini tidak boleh kamu makan, kan?"

that are in this orchard you are not allowed to eat, are you?"

\dt 01/Oct/2009

\c L-03
\t Story 3: JOSEPH - INTRODUCTION
\stg Expl. (Lo'am) JP
\co Language: Lo'am (plm)
\co Reason: Betrayal (introduction)
\co Crafter: Dona (04-April-2009)
\co Backtranslator:
\co Test 1: Agus (27-May-2009)
\co Test 2: Wida (27-Jul-2009)
\co Sources used in crafting: audio, DVD, Read'n Grow Picture Bible, Disscussions


\gtst Was there anything surprising or strange in this story?  (If so, tell more about it.)
\gtstid Ada yang mengejutkan atau heran di kisah ini? (Kalau ada, ceritakanlah tentang itu.)
\ansplm 1 - Aneh: Matoari, bulan seblas bintang sembah samo dio.
\ans 1 - Strange: The sun, the moon and eleven stars worship him.
\ansid 2 - Agak rumit.
\ans 2 - Rather complex.

\gtst Was there anything you particularly liked or disliked about this story? Or something that made an
impression on you?  (If so, tell more about it.)
\gtstid Ada yang khususnya disukai atau tidak disukai tentang kisah ini?  Atau sesuatu yang mengesankan
(Kalau ada, ceritakanlah tentang itu.)
\ansplm 1 - Bagus galo
\ans 1 - Everything's fine.
\ansid 2 - Kelebihan dari Nabi Yusup kepada kakak-kakak, karena mimpinya.
\ans 2 - Speciality of Nabi Yusup over the older brothers, because of his dreams.

\gtst Does this remind you of a story or event that you've heard from your own cultural context?  (If so, tell
more about it.)
\gtstid Apakah ini memperingatkan tentang kisah atau peristiwa yang didengar dari budaya Babak/Ibu
sendiri? (Kalau ada, ceritakanlah tentang itu.)
\ansplm 1 - Pernah, samo guru agama.
\ans 1 - Already, from the religion teacher.
\ansid 2 - Belum pernah dengar cerita ini atau mirip.
\ans 2 - I never heard this story or a similar one.

\gtst What do you think is the point of this story?  
\gtstid Apa topik kasih ini menurut Bapak/Ibu?
\ansplm 1 - Jangan nyuruh bapa, mama nyujud samo dio.
\ans 1 - One should not tell dad and mom to worship him.
\ansid 2 - Kebaikan. Walaupun kelebihan Nabi Yusup, dia masih rendah hati, tidak sombong.
\ans 2 - Kindness. Despite the speciality of Nabi Yusup, he remained humble, not proud.

\gtst Who is the hero or villain in the story?
\gtstid Siapakah pahlawan (yang baik) atau siapakah penjahat (yang jahat) di kisah ini?
\ansplm 1 - Yang baik, adek. Yang jahat kakaknyo karno iri.
\ans 1 - The good guy, the younger brother. The bad guys, his older brothers because they were jealous.
\ansid 2 - Yang baik: Nabi Yusup. Kakak-kakak hanya iri.
\ans 2 - The good: Nabi Yusup. The older brothers are just jealous.

\gtst Does this story seem like it could have actually happened (is true), or does it seem far-fetched (untrue)
or like a fable?  Why do you think this?
\gtstid Apakah kisah ini tampaknya sungguh-sungguh terjadi (kisah benar), atau tampaknya tidak menyakinkan
(kisah tak benar) atau tampaknya seperti dongeng? Mengapa?
\ansplm 1 - Sungguh-sungguh.
\ans 1 - Truly.
\ansid 2 - Seperti dongeng juga. Karena mimpi: Ikat gandum dan bintang/matahari.
\ans 2 - Like a tale too. Because of the dreams: binding wheat and stars/sun.


\ln 03.01
\nat Cerito ini dimulai dari Adam.
\bt Cerita ini dimulai dari Adam.
\en This story was started from Adam.
\anc gen.05:01

\ln 03.02
\nat Itu punya keturunan.
\bt Itu punya keturunan.
\en That had descendants.
\anc gen.05:01 - gen.05:32, gen.11:10 - gen.11:26

\ln 03.03
\nat Keturunan namonyo Ibrahim.
\bt Keturunan namonyo Ibrahim.
\en The desecendant his name was Ibrahim.
\anc gen.11:26

\ln 03.04
\nat Ibrahim tu punyo anak. Namonyo Ishak.
\bt Ibrahim itu punya anak. Namanya Ishak.
\en That Ibrahim had a child. His name was Ishak.
\anc gen.17:19

\ln 03.05
\nat Dari Ishak ni dilahirkelah Yakup.
\bt Dari Ishak ni dilahirkan Yakup.
\en From this Ishak it was born Yakup.
\anc gen.25:26
\tst How many generations do you think are between Adam and Yakup?
\ansplm 1 - Empat. Karno keturunan samo dengen anak. Aman lebih jauh cucung.
\ans 1 - Four. Because descendant is the same like child. If farther it's grandchild.
\ansid 2 - Empat generasi.
\ans 2 - Four generations.

\ln 03.06
\nat Na, Yakup ni punyo duoblas iko anak.
\bt Na, Yakup ini punya dua belas orang anak.
\en Well, this Yakup had twelve children.
\anc gen.35:22

\ln 03.07
\nat Dari duoblas iko anak ini ado siko anak lain disayanglah dio samo siko anak ni, namonyo Yusup.
\bt Dari dua belas orang anak ini ada seorang anak lain disayang oleh dia dengan seorang anak ini,
namanyo Yusup.
\en From these twelve children there was another child, it was loved by him this child, his name
was Yusup.
\anc gen.37:03

\ln 03.08
\nat Waktu Yusup itu umurnyolah tujuhblas taun, itulah mulailah nggembalake biri-biri di padang rumput
samo kakak-kakaknyo yang ado di sano. Na.
\bt Waktu Yusup itu umurnya tujuh belas tahun, dia mulai menggembalakn domba di padang rumput
dengan kakak-kakanya yang ada di sana. Na.
\en When that Yusup was seventeen years old, he began to herd sheep on the pasture with his
older brothers that were there. Well.
\anc gen.37:02

\ln 03.09
\nat Lajukelah dilaporkenyo pulo ke bapaknyo itu gawe kakak-kakaknyo itu yang ado di padang rumput itu tu.
\bt Terus dilaporkannya juga kepada bapaknya itu pekerjaan kakak-kakaknya itu yang ada di padang
rumput itu.
\en Then it was also reported to his father the work of those his older brothers that were on that
pasture.
\anc gen.37:02
\tst What do you think these brothers do there? Why would Yusup have to report it?
\ansplm 1 - Ado jail. Ado keslahan.
\ans 1 - There is naughtyness. There are mistakes.
\ansid 2 - Nakal atau jahil samo dio, karno dak sukak samo dio.
\ans 2 - Naughty or foolish with him, because they didn't like him.

\ln 03.10
\nat Tambah lagi si Yakup itu ngunjukke baju yang bagus pulo untuk Yusup.
\bt Tambah lagi si Yakup itu memberikan baju yang bagus juga untuk Yusup.
\en In addition that Yakup also gave a good coat to Yusup.
\anc gen.37:03
\tst What kind of dress (coat) could that have been?
\ansplm 1 - Ado sorban. Panjang. Bukan baju dalam.
\ans 1 - There is a turban. Long. Not underware.
\ansid 2 - Mungkin juba, yang panjang. Jaman dulu.
\ans 2 - Maybe a robe, a long one. Old times. 

\ln 03.11
\nat Kakak-kakak ni dak senang galo nyingok si Yusup ini ni.
\bt Kakak-kakak ini tidak senang sama sekali melihat si Yusup ini.
\en These older brothers were not glad at all to see this Yusup.
\anc gen.37:04

\ln 03.12
\nat Suatu hari mimpilah pulo si Yusup ini, diceritokenyolah samo kakak-kakaknyo:
\bt Suatu hari bermimpi juga si Yusup ini, diceritakannya kepada kakak-kakaknya.
\en One day this Yusup also had a dream, it was told to his older brothers.
\anc gen.37:05, gen.37:06

\ln 03.13
\nat "Ado di ladang itu kito tu ngikat batang gandum galo, tapi ikatan batang gandum Yusup itu yang paling
tinggi dari pado yang lainnyo.
\bt "Ada di ladang itu kita itu mengikat batang gadnum semua, tetapi ikatan batang gandum Yusup
itu yang paling tinggi daripada yang lainnya.
\en "it was on that field we all were binding wheat stalks, but that bundle of wheat stalk of Yusup
was the highest of all the others.
\anc gen.37:07

\ln 03.14
\nat Dan ikatan gandum kakak-kakaknyo sujud nyembah ikatan gandum si Yusup ini."
\bt Dan ikatan gandum kakak-kakaknya sujud menyembah ikatan gadnum si Yusup ini."
\en And the wheat stalks of his older brothers bowed worshipping this wheat stalk of Yusup."
\anc gen.37:07
\tst Why do you think did Yusup tell them the dream?
\ansplm 1 - Supaya kakak-kakak tau. Curhat.
\ans 1 - In order that the older brothers know. Pour out the heart (=open the heart)
\ansid 2 - Mungkin Yusup pikir ini tunjukan dari Tuhan mau membuat Yusup Nabi.
\ans 2 - Maybe Yusup thought it was a sign from God that He wants to make Yusup become a prophet.

\tst What do you think he expected
\ansplm 1 - Tidak mikirke, kagek kakak2 marah.
\ans 1 - (He was) not thinking, later his older brothers became angry
\ansid 2 - Di sini mungkin hanya cerita. Dengan mimpi yang kedua mungkin baru sadar mau dibuat nabi samo
Tuhan.
\ans 2 - Here maybe only a story. Maybe only with the second dream he was aware the he will be made a
prophet by God.

\ln 03.15
\nat Laju kato kakak-kakaknyo:
\bt Terus kata kakak-kakaknya:
\en Then said his older brothers:
\anc gen.37:08

\ln 03.16
\nat "Apo kau pikir kau merintah pucuk kami?
\bt "Apaka kamu berpikir kamu memerintah di atas kami?
\en "Do you think you rule over us?
\anc gen.37:08

\ln 03.17
\nat Apo kau pikir kau tu jadi rajo pucuk kami pulo?"
\bt Apa kamu berpikir kamu itu menjadi raja di atas kami juga?
\en Do you think you become king over us, too?"
\anc gen.37:08
\tst Why do you think were they reacting like that.
\ansplm 1 - Dio takut kagek jadi nyato.
\ans 1 - They were afraid it could become true.
\ansplm 2 - Udah idak senang somo dio. Mungkin takut mimpi jadi penyatoan.
\ans 2 - Not happy anymore with him. Maybe they're afriad the dream could become true.

\ln 03.18
\nat Na, dari situ tambah dak sukolah kakak-kakak si Yusup ini samo dio.
\bt Na, dari situ bertambah tidak suka kakak-kakak si Yusup ini dengan dia.
\en Well, from there it increased not liking him these older brothers of Yusup.
\anc gen.37:08 

\ln 03.19
\nat Sesudah itu mimpi lagi pulo si Yusup ini. Dio ngomongke cak ini na:
\bt Sesudah itu bermimpi lagi juga si Yusup ini. Dia berkata begini:
\en After that this Yusup had another dream, too. He said like this:
\anc gen.37:094

\ln 03.20
\nat "Kalo matoari, bulan samo seblas bintang tu sujud pulo nyembah dio."
\bt "Kalau matahari, bulan dan sebelas bintang itu sujud juga menyembah dia."
\en "As for the sun, the moon and those eleven stars also bowed worshipping him."
\anc gen.37:09
\tst What do you think does that mean?
\ansplm 1 - Matoari = bapa, bulan = mama, seblas bintang = kakaknyo
\ans 1 - Sun = dad, moon = mum, eleven stars = his older brothers
\ansid 2 - Mungkin petunjuk dari Tuhan Yusup jadi Nabi. Mungkin Tuhan suruh matoari, bulan samo seblas
bintang sujud samo dio.
\ans 2 - Maybe this is a sign from God that Yusup will become a prophet. Maybe God commands the sun, the
moon and eleven stars to worship him.

\ln 03.21
\nat Laju didatengi Yakuplah si Yusup itu, ditanyoke si Yakup:
\bt Terus didatangi Yakuplah si Yusup itu, ditanyakan si Yakup:
\en Then it was visited by Yakup that Yusup, it was asked by Yakup:
\anc gen.37:10

\ln 03.22
\nat "Yusup, nurut kau, apo ubak, umak, samo kakak-kakak ni sujud galo nyembah kau?."
\bt "Yusup, menurut kamu, apakah bapak, ibu, dan kakak-kakak ini sujud semua menyembah kamu?."
\en "Yusup, according to you, do dad, mam and these older brothers all bow worshipping you?"
\anc gen.37:10
\tst How do you think did Yusup's father's reaction look like?
\ansplm 1 - Marah, negur dio. Takut jadi nyato.
\ans 1 - Angry, rebuke him. Afraid, it will happen.
\ansid 2 - Mungkin dia senang anak jadi Nabi, tapi belum pasti tau, karno itu nanyo samo Yusup.
\ans 2 - Maybe he was happy that his son will become a prophet, but he di not know for sure, because of that
he asked Yusup.

\ln 03.23
\nat Na. Laju kakak-kakak itu tambah bencilah nyingok si Yusup.
\bt Na. Terus kakak-kakak itu tambah benci melihat si Yusup.
\en Well. Then those older brothers increasingly hated to see Yusup.
\anc gen.37:11

\ln 03.24
\nat Tapi disimpan Yakup apo yang jadi mimpi si Yusup di dalem hatinyo.
\bt Tetapi disimpan oleh Yakup apa yang menjadi mimpi si Yusup in his heart.
\en But it was stored by Yakup what became the dreams of Joseph in his heart.
\anc gen.37:11

\dt 28/Sep/2009

\c T-00
\t Tharaka Story Set & Mini-bios
\stg Bkgrnd (Tharaka) BK
\bt Redemptive Theme
\co Our redemptive theme is relationships with forgiveness as a sub-theme. (Mbuthia) 
\co The Tharaka people value relationships very much. To them every elder is either a father or a mother
and they so often call one another brother. They really respect their family lines and clans such that
there are clans that one is allowed to marry from and those that do not trade with the other. The theme
on relationship would help strengthen what they already have and also insist on the Importance of
relating well with people outside their clans. Jesus came to reconcile / restore the broken relationship
between God and man. Forgiveness is the tool that God used to restore this broken relationship when he
send his son to die for the sin of all mankind.

 

\bt Info about team (gender, age, education, believer?, etc.)
\co Mini-bio about Crafters:

\co Japheth Nyaga:  A man in the 40s. He is married and with two (2) children. He is a primary school
teacher and with a very good understanding of the Bible. He has been our only story crafter until we got
Laban Muriungi. He crafted stories with alot of ease. He is a native Tharaka speaker with a very good
command in the language .Later on, he became so unavailable for us. For this and other reasons we
decided not to continue using him for crafting. We however keep touch with Him and his family.
Japheth has been a believer for years earlier. He goes to church once in a while but his lifestyle has
really changed and he no longer keeps the conduct expected of believers. We pray for him that he may
reconsider his ways and make the right turn for life. We also used Him to test some stories. 

\co Laban Muriungi-  Young man in his early 20s, A recent High School leaver, A committed Christian and
he is quite commited reader of the Tharaka New testament and other versions of the Bible. He is quite
good in his choice of word.He translates words from English or Swahili to Tharaka with very little
difficulty. He is very coo[perative and accepts correction without taking offence. He is quite busy
because He works as a teacher in a local secondary school. However he avails Himself almost every
time we need him. we sometimes use him to back translate. 

\co Gerald King'ori-A married man with one daughter. He is a believer and a frequent bible reader. He
engages in a lot of reading and study. He is a native Tharaka speaker and is very good in translating the
words to come up with the right Tharaka word that is easily understood. He is a class 8 graduate and
quite informed. We are training him to do story crafting and he seems to be getting it quite fast. we
thank God for him.

\co Sabina Gaake.- She is a young single lady who is believer and very active in the church. She is a Form
4 graduate and a native Tharaka speaker with a good command in English, Swahili and Tharaka. She
does printing and typing as a source of income. She however moved from Tharaka and we can nolonger
use her to do back translations. We also used her to test some stories.
