\dt 28/Sep/2009

\c T-07
\t Jacob Wrestles with God.
\stg S-by-S (Tharaka) BK
\co Tharaka
\co The main reason to have this story is to bring out and show who the people we call the Israelites are and
where they came from.
\co Crafter: Laban Muriungi
\co Backtranslator: Shadrack
\co Test 1: John-A young man who is a believer. Quit versed with the Bible and understands a great deal of
Tharaka too. He learned the story but had a problem remembering the last line of the Story.
\co Test 2: Michael Nyaga- A believer that is quite conversant with the both the bible and issues to do with
the Tharaka culture and language. He learned the story quitewell but had a problem remembering the last
line of the Story.
\ln 07.01
\bt After Abraham died, God blessed his son Isaac with many blessings,
\anc gen.25:11
\tst Why do you think God blessed Isaac?
\ans God was commited to fullfil  His promise. He had promised to bless Abraham with many blessings.
\rtl1 After Abraham had died, God blessed Isaac with very many blessings.
\rtl2 After Abraham had died God blessed Isaac with children.
\ln 07.02
\bt And Isaac lived with his children for a long time.
\anc gen.27:02
\rtl1 Isaac lived with His children for  a long time.
\rtl2
\ln 07.03
\bt One day Isaac called one of his sons called Jacob and Blessed Him.
\anc gen.28:01
\tst How would one person bless the other?
\ans By saying good things about a person. A father can call his favourite child and give him instructions
about how the home should be run after his death. This too is blessing.
\tst Among the Tharaka people who does the blessing?
\ans An elder can call a younger person to bless him/her. Only an older person can bless.-the one being
blessed should be younger.
\ans
\rtl1 One day Isaac called his child called Jacob and told him,
\rtl2 One day Isaac called one of his sons, Jacob,
\ln 07.04
\bt He told him, "Do not marry any of these Cannanite women
\anc gen.28:01
\tst Why do you think Isaac told Jacob not to marry  the Caananite women?
\ans It may be because of cultural differences. May be he disliked the way they carried themselves/ how
they behaved.
\rtl1 "Do not marry a woman from town of Canaan.
\rtl2 He told him, "Do not marry from this generationof Canaanites
\ln 07.05
\bt but go to the home of your uncle Laban and marry one of his daughters.
\anc gen.28:02
\tst Do parents have a say on who should be married by their children?
\ans Yes. They give restrictions on the clans that someone should not marry from. This is because of enemity
between diferent clans or some oaths taken by their forefathers.
\rtl1 go to your uncle and marry one of his daughters"
\rtl2 Go to your uncle Laban's place and marry a girl from there.
\cn In Tharaka and many of the Kenyan cultures one is not allowed to marry his uncle's daughter. This is a
cousin and therefore a close relative.
\ln 07.06
\bt May the Lord give you the blessings that He promised to Abraham,
\anc gen.28:04
\tst
\rtl1
\rtl2
\ln 07.07
\bt May He give you this land where we live as if it does not belong to us to be yours"
\anc gen.28:04
\tst what does it mean to live in a land as if it is not yours (like a foreigner)?
\ans
\rtl1
\rtl2
\cn These lines , 07.06 and 07.07 were skipped in the recording of the stories used for testing. We feel
that they are important as they explain the reason why God would have blessed Jacob. It would be good
if they are part of the story and quite easy to remember. The story has already been edited to include
the lines.
\ln 07.08
\bt Jacob went to the home of Laban where he lived for many years.
\anc gen.31:38
\tst What  do you think Jacob was doing in Laban's home for the many years he lived there?
\ans He may have had a place to cultivate and produce wealth. This is because He was rich when coming out
of the land.
\rtl1 Jacob went to Laban's place and stayed there for a long time.
\rtl2 Jacob went to his uncle Laban's place and stayed there for many years.
\ln 07.09
\bt God blessed him with alot of things/wealth, wives, children, and workers (Servants).
\anc gen.31:01
\tst How can God bless someone with such things? Are all blessings tangible?
\ans God can bless someone with such blessings if he/she is obedient  to God and hardworking. Not all
blessings are tangible.
\rtl1 where God blessed him with a wife, children and alot of wealth
\rtl2 And God blessed Him With wealth.
\cn The Tharaka word used for wealth is the same one used for things and properties. The backtranslator
therefore gave both alternatives but in the story it is clear that the crafter meant wealth.
\ln 07.10
\bt One day God appeared to Jacob and told Him, " Return to the country of your origin,
\anc Gen.31:03
\tst How does God speak to people? Has He ever spoken to you?
\ans God would make something to happen and the interpretation of this will convey the message from God.
\ans Through prophets, dreams and answers to prayers.
\rtl1 One day God appeared to him and told him, "return to the land you had come from"
\rtl2 Jacob, one day God spoke to him and told him to go back
\ln 07.11
\bt the country of your fathers, the country of your family, the country of your people".
\anc Gen.31:03,Gen.31:13
\tst Which country/ land is God reffering to in this story (the one that Jacob is returning to)?
\ans This is the land where his father lived.
\rtl1
\rtl2 to  the land of his fathers, their home and the place of His people.
\ln 07.12
\bt Jacob gathered all things that God had blessed Him with, wives , children, and workers and they
started the Journey to the country of his origin.
\anc Gen.31:17, Gen.31:18
\tst How could you describe the journey that Jacob and those with him are taking?
\ans It must have been a long journey that took many days because of the many things they were carrying

\c z-97
\t ONESTORY TOOLBOX HELPS
\co TO ADD A NEW STORY RECORD: 
\co2 1. place the cursor in the ProjectBT window, click on Database / Insert Record. 
\co2 2. It will ask you for the Record you want to insert--so you should write a new chapter number (be sure
to insert a zero before single digit numbers)--try to estimate where the story will come in your story set.
\co2 3. Click ok. 
\co2 4. A new record will open and you can begin to key in the story and anchors. 
\co2 4. The template will automatically give you 30 linenumbers. You can change them from "02.xx" to
whatever chapter number you gave, by using Edit / Replace. Make sure that you leave the period after
the number.
\co2 5. Choose the "replace all" button. Hit "ok".

\co TO SEE YOUR WHOLE LIST OF STORIES
\co2 1. If you want to see titles as well as chapter numbers, click on View / Browse Fields.  A window will
open up with a list of all available fields. Highlight "t" and click "last" to move it to the right.
\co2 2. Click "ok"
\co2 3. Click on the three-column icon above to see an index of your stories -- both chapter numbers and
titles.

\co TO ADD A FIELD:  
\co2 1. Click on Enter, and then "\"-- this brings up a list of Standard Format markers that this window can
use. 
\co2 2. Click on the marker you want, hit space and your cursor will be back in the window you can write in.

\co TO DELETE A RECORD:  
\co2 1. VERY IMPORTANT:  Click in the window of the record you want to delete.  
\co2 2. Click on Database / Delete record
\co2 3. Select "yes"

\co TO ARRANGE YOUR WINDOWS:  
\co2 1. Click on Window
\co2 2. Choose the type of arrangement you want for your windows (cascade, tile, tile side by side) -- OR just
drag each window to where you want it, and then resize it to fit.

\co TO SEND A BACKTRANSLATION RECORD TO A CONSULTANT:  
\co2 1. Click in the back-translation window 
\co2 2. Click on File / Export - select "standard format" and select "show properties dialog box on export" 
\co2 3. Click on the "export" button - another window will open.  If the "consistent changes" field has
anything in it, make it blank.
\co2 4. Hit the "browse" button on the "output file" field - another window will open 
\co2 5. Give your file a name with a ".txt" extension and hit save. 
\co2 6. Go to your email program and create a new email to your consultant.  Attach the file that you just
exported from Toolbox.

\co TO ADD A RECORD FROM A CONSULTANT:  
\co2 1. Double-click on e-mail attachment to open it.  
\co2 2. Select all the text in the document.  
\co2 3. Copy the highlighted text. 
\co2 4. Click in the Consultant Notes window in Toolbox 
\co2 5. Go to the record number that you are working with - highlight the entire record. 
\co2 6. Paste to replace the old copy of the file with the new updated one.

\co TO SEND A CONSULTANT NOTES FILE BACK TO THE CONSULTANT (with your answers in it)
\co2 1. Click in the ConNotes window
\co2 2. Hit "file", then "export" - select "standard format" and select "show properties dialog box on export" 
\co2 3. Hit the "export" button - another window will open.  Make the "consistent changes" field blank. 
\co2 4. Hit the "browse" button on the "output file" field - another window will open 
\co2 6. Go to your email program and create a new email to your consultant.  Attach the file that you just
exported from Toolbox.


\ln line number--this should match the line number in the ConNotes file, use the format xx.xx   

\ln To JUMP from the 
\ln field in this window to the equivalent 
\ln field in the ConNotes window, rightclick on the number.
\bt backtranslation (keep your lines fairly short)
\bt to JUMP: From this line you can jump to records you have made in the keyterms database. For
example, if this line had the word "God" in it, and if you have made a keyterm record called
"God", then a rightclick on the word "God" will immediately bring up the record in the keyterms
database.
\anc anchor ref -- If you are working with a language for which there is translated scripture with
a backtraslation, it would be helpful to your consultant for you to paste the BT of the
appropriate vss.
\anc to JUMP from anc to NETBIBLE rightclick on the reference here (eg. Gen.01:01) and your
cursor will immediately bring up the verse in the Netbible window
\cn Crafting note -- put cultural info here, or reasons why you crafted the story in a certain way, or
information about this line from your testing groups.
\cn to JUMP: From this line you can also reference records you have made of Cultural observations. For
example, if this line of the story is about the Wedding at Cana, and you have made observations about
weddings in the group you work with, A rightclick on the word Wedding will jump to the "Wedding"
record in the Cultural notes database. (Note that in order for the jump to work, the Cultural Notes
database needs to be sorted by \r)
\tst testing question -- prepare testing questions ahead of time.  Then put the response here
also.
\old A preivous version of this line of this line of the story.  As you proceed through testing and
editing of the story you occasionally decide to delete a line or to make major changes. If
you do that, we'd like for you to keep old versions of each line--especially if there have
been consultant comments about it.
\dt 01/Oct/2009

\co Language: Naya
\co Reason for including story: Shows the beginning of man beging separated from God and His holiness.
Prophesies the coming of Jesus from the beginning of time.
\co Crafter: Grandma Charley, Aug 13, 2009
\co Resources used in story: 3 BI recordings (Context., BISS, ITB), listened 6 times to the story. No other
resources used. Recordings done in a studio for us in Medan.
\co BTer: Eli & Naomi, a husband and wife who have no children. He is very knowledgable about his faith.
The two of them plan on making the hajj for the first time this year.
\co Yellow highlights missing info; green highlights incorrect or confusing info

\ln 02.23
\ind Matu'ai iye, niba Tuhan Halik ia mek sira ba'doda/bahayanda niadei'ein Tuhan tenek beibeik
ayou-ayou singa tek bahak banonda souk iye a.  Sesudah itu, Tuhan Halik diberikan kepada mereka
pakaian dibuat Tuhan dari kulit kayu yang ada di dalam negeri ini.
\bt After that, Lord Creator was given unto them clothes made by Lord from wood skin which is
inside this country.
\anc Gen.03:21 But wrong detail there

\ln 02.24
\ind Matu'ai iye, niba sao pedang mek sebelah barat siuk nan iye mata balal gunone manjago veirei sia akeun
mek taneum-taneumen singa vadou raik nian ia. Sesudah itu, dikasih satu pedang sebelah barat sesudah
itu nanti matahari gunanya supaya jangan sampai dekat kepada tanaman yang terlarang makan itu.
\bt After that, is given one sword west side after that next sun its use/purpose so that don't reach
close unto plant which forbidden eat that one.
\anc Gen.03:24 for the sword, but the west and the sun and forbidden plant are not anchorable.

\ln 02.25
\ind Mangkoune, ek siraya sa'a mahawali sia balanjoda ek banon singa nitantukeun Tuhan Halik ia. Makanya,
mereka mencari nafka di tempat yang ditentukan Tuhan Halik itu.
\bt So, they searched basic life necesseties at place which fixed/determined by that Lord Creator.
\anc Gen.03:23 kind of
